I think there is a perception that it's like ripping off a band-aid and that it should be done quickly to be less painful, but I find it less painful and more thorough with a slower speed.   93. I have owned a few epilators, though not many. I should start out by saying that epilation isn't exactly my favorite hair removal method. It is time-consuming (you have to go over areas several times), uncomfortable (don't let anyone lie to you), and if you neglect to exfoliate, you will end up with ugly, painful, ingrown hairs, which can even scar if you don't take care of them properly. However, there is something very attractive about a hair removal method that you can do at home, won't cost an arm an a leg (have you priced waxing lately?), and you don't have to do it every day. So if you haven't been scared away, this epilator is by far the best I've tried. MICROVIBRATIONS!!! They are awesome!!! They really do cut down on the discomfort. It feels a bit weird at first, but it is a happy distraction from the root-ripping occurring in very sensitive areas! It works well wet or dry, although I find I miss more spots if I use it in the bath/shower. Enter the Smartlight!!! Nothing gets by this thing. Even in a well-lit environment, you can really miss a lot without this nifty light. I also like the two-speed option . . . sometimes faster isn't always better, especially in tender places. Ditto to the exfoliating brush . . . don't neglect to use it or something like it or you will pay with nasty, bumpy ingrown hairs. My only gripe with this device is the battery life. It would be nice to be able to finish the job in one sitting, and this falls short for me. It lasts about 45 minutes on average . . . maybe a little longer on the slower speed. With as many times as I have to go over areas to get everything the Smartlight illuminates and really do a good job, I maybe finish a leg and a half before it dies. A little longer life would be appreciated. Along the lines of battery life . . . it charges fairly quickly, so it's not THAT awful to wait until the battery is charged again. I recall reading reviews about the cord not plugging in securely to the device--on my device, I found you have to push quite firmly until you hear it snap in place . . . then it definitely stays put. All-in-all, this is a pretty solid product.

I have extremely sensitive skin, so I always had to splurge and get the ~16-18 dollar packs of razors with some kind of soap on the razor head (Generally the Venus + Olay mix). Every time the soap ran out, I had to put on a new head - I was pretty much just throwing money at these companies. I was looking into cheaper alternatives, and then I found out about epilating. I bought this at around $75, and I figured even if it only lasted me a year or two, I was still saving money in the long run.<br /><br />I'm not going to lie - this HURTS the first time you do it. Since I had been shaving for over 10 years, my skin was not at all prepared to have the hairs ripped out. But, I've had my epilator for about 2 weeks now, and it really does get easier.<br /><br />I highly recommend that before the first time you epilate, you get the places you aim to epilate waxed at a salon. I wish I had done this, as this helps your skin get used to it all at once. When the hairs are pulled out, as opposed to being shaved, it takes much longer to grow back, and they also grow back thinner and finer. I'm not saying these hairs will be baby soft now, but they will be easier to epilate.<br /><br />Now, the best way to epilate. From my experience as a complete beginner, the wet/dry feature of this is what makes this process possible for me. Generally, what I have found to work is to epilate everything you want in the shower. I do legs, underarms, and some pubic area. So, when I'm in the shower, I'll make sure the stream of water (try to do hot water while you are getting used to this) is over the place I am about to epilate, and then I'll do a couple swipes. You probably won't get all of the hair, but that's okay - I've noticed it takes a few times to get it all. Then, the day after you have done this process, I recommend the next day epilating your legs while they are dry. The light feature on this epilator is SO convenient - it really helps you see any small hairs you might have missed. I recommend putting a towel down, putting a movie on, and focus on getting as much of the hair as you can. It's going to sting, but not as much as you think it will while doing it dry.<br /><br />Despite how much of a pain it might seem at first, it's really worth it.

Some quick thoughts on this model specifically:<br />* Removes smaller hairs (0.5mm) than older models, so you can be more aggressive as stray hairs start to grow back<br />* The \\"massagers\\" on the epilation head really do help<br />* You can use it dry or completely-wet, but not damp (e.g., right after the shower won't work)... and I must say that using it under running water dramatically reduces any discomfort, although it's a bit harder to notice stray hairs<br />* You can't use it while plugged in (that would be a serious safety hazard in the shower!) but it means that whenever the battery eventually stops holding a charge, you'll have to toss the unit)<br />* I wish this included a trimming head like other models, for the cases when you have longer hairs you want to attack (they have to be 7 mm or shorter before this will really pull them out)<br />* This doesn't include an attachment for facial hair like some do (which is OK)... just make sure that your epilator is clean if you're going to use it on your face, because otherwise it will make you break out<br />* The small spotlight on the unit makes it much easier to see hairs you may have missed<br />* The exfoliating brush is a nice touch, because epilating frequently leads to ingrown hairs. It says to use it a day or two before epilating, and it's super-gentle... almost feels like it's not doing anything, but I found it's more effective and more comfortable (if more slow) than just using a loofah. The \\"wait 2 days\\" advice is good because otherwise your skin gets sensitive<br /><br />And some thoughts on epilation in general:<br />* This seems obvious, but I have to say it: it only hurts when a hair is being removed. This means that the first time you epilate, it's very uncomfortable. But since only a small percentage of the hair grows back before you epilate again (assuming you do it at least once every 3 months!), the subsequent touch-ups really aren't bad at all, especially on your legs. (Underarms are less comfortable, and bikini area even less so. Face is also quite sensitive, though that probably varies by person, depending on how much tweezing you normally do.)<br />* The first time you epilate, your legs will be unbelievably smooth. But hair grows back at different rates, so after a month or so of epilating (maybe one time each week), you'll have tiny hairs here and there, that are starting to grow back but are still too small to get. It's less of an issue with this epilator than others, and the hairs aren't really visible. So if you think someone's going to be touching your legs, then shave :-D but otherwise life is much easier if you just epilate once a week or so. Then if you don't bother doing anything for a month or so, you'll have a few stray hairs here and there, but nothing like someone who shaves regularly and then skips a month (or even a week... or even 3 days). Visible stubble is entirely a thing of the past.<br />* Remember that the exfoliation is important to prevent ingrown hairs (just little bumps on your legs--mine don't turn red). But if you wax, or if you age ;) you'll have to do that anyway. And this unit's exfoliator is more gentle than a loofah<br />* And how could I forget the #1 reason to epilate: no more underarm bumps. You know, the ones that you ALWAYS have, despite a million products on the market that say they'll banish them but don't? Sometimes when you epilate, your skin will be red for 30-90 seconds afterward, but then it fades. So NO MORE BUMPS. That alone is reason enough to own an epilator, IMO :) This also helps with bikini-area bumps, but I find in those cases that the redness can take several hours to fade, so it's fantastic to use the day before swimming but would not be a good choice immediately before pool time

  270. I'm new to epilation (a couple of months in). I tried an inexpensive, corded Remington, and after the initial painfest, decided I like this method of hair removal. I was afraid of getting ingrown hairs, though, so the exfoliating brush on this Braun was appealing to me, as was its promise of removing hairs as short as .5 mm.<br /><br />I quickly realized that the exfoliating brush is a joke. They say it will \\"exfoliate your skin 4X more effectively than manually scrubbing,\\" which I imagined as being the mechanically spinning brush versus a typical manual exfoliation technique, such as scrubbing yourself with a loofah. No, now I'm pretty sure they mean that this is four times as effective when it's turned on as it would be if you just manually scrubbed the brush around without power. So that's not really saying much. The bristles are very soft (I wouldn't hesitate to use this on my face, not that it would be of any benefit), and even with holding the running appliance in the same spot for a long time, I couldn't tell that it had done anything. Afterwards, my skin felt no different. It still felt bumpy from ingrown hairs. I tried the brush wet, dry, with shower gel...it made no difference. Then I put on my dollar-store shower gloves and gave my legs a brisk rubdown...problem solved. The bristles, by the way, do NOT spin or rotate, nor does the head. The whole thing just kind of shimmies. It turns out that there is NO spinning action whatsoever. So I pronounce the brush on this thing as a worthless gimic that drives up the price.<br /><br />However, I did find that this Braun removed shorter hairs than the Remington. And because it is cordless, it was more convenient to use. The battery holds a long charge (it never ran down on me), and now, using this Braun in conjunction with my shower gloves, I'm very pleased with the smoothness of my legs.<br /><br />As another reviewer suggested, I took off the pivoting head. The \\"massage\\" function is also a joke(it makes absolutely no difference in the perception of pain), and the rollers on the head rattle disconcertingly (makes it sound like my father's gas-powered lawn edger), and they interfere with the smooth movement of the device over your skin (you have to fight against the rollers, which make the device want to move in only one direction). Removing the head also allowed me to remove much shorter hairs. I was terrified at first, afraid it would allow the tweezers to pinch me, but that wasn't a problem at all. Well, not until I tried epilating my upper inner thighs, where yo-yo dieting and age have left the skin less than taut. Yeouch! When doing areas with looser skin, put the head back on! And don't forget to stretch that skin tight!<br /><br />If you're new to epilating, you may find the experience so painful that you wonder if it's just from tweezing or if your skin is being pinched. Trust me, you will KNOW. Pinched skin will develop tiny little pinprick red spots (and may actually bleed). Painfully epilated (but unpinched) skin might have a diffuse redness, but no pinpricks.<br /><br />Actually, I'm surprised by how short of hairs this thing can get without pinching the skin. I'm impressed with that aspect.<br /><br />I found the wet/dry functionality to not be very helpful. This thing just works better dry, plain and simple, and epilating wet (or submerged) was no less painful.<br /><br />The name of the \\"smartlight\\" is kind of silly. There is nothing \\"smart\\" about it. It's just a light. But calling it \\"smart\\" makes it sound high-tech and worthy of a higher price. I don't think I really need it, but every now it illuminates some hairs I didn't realize were there, so I guess it's a feature worth having (but not overly so).<br /><br />Overall, I think this Braun was not worth its premium price, because the cost-inflating features just aren't worth it. I would recommend one of the cheaper Brauns that still feature the \\"close-grip technology,\\" perhaps something like the [[ASIN:B0077PLO60 Braun 5-5280 ]], which is currently about $30 less than I paid for this model, yet also has attachments you might actually find useful, such as a shaver and a trimmer cap. You could do much worse than this Braun, and I must admit I'm very pleased with the end results, but I think most people choose this specific model for the exfoliating brush, which I found to be a mistake.

I have never used an epilator. This is my personal experience as an Epilating Virgin. I suffer from ingrown hairs on the outer part of my lower legs (below knee). I carefully unpacked the package, Braun epilation wipes, read the instructions/care manual and charged my new device for a bit. I couldn't wait for too long so I cleaned my legs with the wipe. The wipe doesnothing but clean your legs and make them smell great. Seems a very 'placeboish' product. I read up on online forums and took pain killers because it would supposedly reduce inflammation and pain later on. Now onto the epilating...<br /><br />The sound when turned on is very nerve-wracking even on it's low setting or as I refer to it as, \\"chicken speed\\". It made me nervous and a bit uneasy, but I still braved on! OH MY!! Add a few expletives and constant, OUCHES, OH MY GOD, HOLY HELL and so on and you get my point. I believe that sensation is translating that way because you are tweezing 40 hairs at the same time. The Emjoi has 2-speed options, more power, moves smoother along the skin and removes more hair quicker ... and cost less. Two things that did not matter to me since I would not use it in the shower or bath anyway. In addition, the Emjoi does not have a sonic exfoliation attachment (which again is not an issue because I use a Clarisonic for that).<br /><br />For those of you who have never used an epilator, it is very uncomfortable (if not slightly painful) the first time. And, your legs (for up to 12 hours) will look like they were stabbed repeatedly with an ice pick. So do NOT epilate right before you need nice, smooth legs. The first time also takes a considerable amount of time (i.e., an hour for both legs) to pull ALL of the hairs out. You will also have to go over the same area repeatedly (as it's not like shaving). In addition, all of the hairs do not grow at the same rate/time, so your \\"first\\" time will involve doing it more than one day. I've epilated with my leg hair both short and long. Everyone says to do it with short hair, but personally, it goes much faster and is much easier with longer hair (and it really isn't that much more painful). Another thing, the epilator alone will never make your legs 100% smooth. To get the 100% smoothness on your legs, you will need to epilate over a 1-3 day period and then shave the \\"roughness\\" from the little tiny microscopic hairs that remain. Doing this will give you very smooth legs for at least a week.
  327. I've tried a couple of different types of epilators over the past 15-20 years. While I was usually happy enough with the results, I rarely used them since it always seemed like you had to wait until the hair got long enough for the unit to grip the hair in order to yank it out. And rarely did I really want the hair on my legs to reach that amount of stubble. Not to mention the pain that is involved with epilators. Yes, I am a weenie.<br /><br />This model of the Braun Silk Epil removes much shorter hair. It claims to remove hair that is as short as a grain of sand (0.5mm). I personally find it requires it to be a bit longer than that to grip; but it does do a much better job of reaching short hair than others I've tried. It has a pivoting head which lets it work around all your body contours. A light on the unit allows even the palest, finest hairs to be visible.<br /><br />In addition to hair removal, this epilator refines your skin. A sonic massage system and high-density brush scrub away old skin cells. This exfoliation helps to stimulate the regeneration of surface skin cells in order to create a smoother skin tone. I do notice a bit of a smoother, more even skin tone on my legs now. This sonic massage is my favorite part of the device...in part because I really don't like the tweezing part.<br /><br />This model can be used wet or dry and uses rechargeable batteries rather than a power cord.<br /><br />Unfortunately, I find that it still hurts...although not nearly as much as it used to. With regular use, the hairs on my legs have become fewer. Plus, the already pale fine hair is becoming even thinner and weaker. Braun claims that it will keep your body free of hair for up to 4 weeks. I usually find it to be somewhere in the 2 to 3 week range for me. Still, that's nice for when you're going on vacation or heading off to the beach for a week or two. I allow the growth to get to the slight stubbly stage and then I'm perfectly smooth for a couple of weeks.of weeks.
